This might be necessary, for example, for:&#10;- investment support, that is managed in the form of a negative asset&#10;- assets under construction, if you need to post a subsequent credit memo to the asset under construction after it has already been completely settled.&#10;The indicator is not required, if depreciation below-zero should be calculated for assets in this class.&#10;Note: You are not allowed to set this indicator for depreciation areas, which are defined to manage negative values (such as, depreciation areas for investment support shown on the liabilities side, or areas for transferred reserves).&#10;&#10;Type: Text&#10;Length: 1</Data></Cell>

    <Cell ss:StyleID="s113"><Data ss:Type="String">Changeover Period of Depreciation Key&#10;&#10;Value 000 to 365 allowed.&#10;Period in the changeover year.     <Cell ss:StyleID="s113"><Data ss:Type="String">Repair Asset Link&#10;&#10;The field is used for fixed assets representing repairs. It is used to link sub-repairs to a big repair. It may also identify if the asset is a big repair or sub-repair.&#10;If you use this field in your company code, link the validation keys L_REPARACAO, B_G_REPARACAO, G_REPARACAO to this field (customizing view FIAAPTV_VAL_KEY).&#10;&#10;Example&#10;The value 'BR18/024' is entered into asset A, the value 'SR18/024' is entered into assets B and C.&#10;The value 'BR' may be used to identify asset A as a Big repair (G_REPARACAO) and the value 'SR' may identify assets B and C as sub-repairs (B_G_REPARACAO).&#10;The value '18/024' is the number of the big repair. Because the same value is entered into assets A, B and C, it may be used to identify that sub-repairs B and C are linked to big-repair A (L_REPARACAO).&#10;&#10;Type: Text&#10;Length: 8</Data></Cell>
    <Cell ss:StyleID="s113"><Data ss:Type="String">Land Asset Link&#10;&#10;The value represents the number for a piece of land. The field is used for fixed assets representing a piece of land or buildings that are built on a piece of land. The field lets you link buildings to a corresponding piece of land. If you use this field in your company code, link the validation key L_TERRENOS to this field (customizing view FIAAPTV_VAL_KEY).&#10;Example:&#10;The value '8456' is entered into the fixed asset A identified as piece of land and also into the assets B and C identified as buildings. The value itself represents the number of a piece of land. Because the same value is entered into assets A and B and C, it may be used to identify that buildings B and C are linked to a piece of land A.&#10;Suggestion: Enter the value 8456 in fixed asset A, which is identified as a piece of land, and also in assets B and C, which are buildings.&#10;&#10;Type: Text&#10;Length: 8</Data></Cell>
    <Cell ss:StyleID="s113"><Data ss:Type="String">Asset Report Form Category&#10;&#10;The field is used to determine Asset Category for Biological and Investment assets. The Asset Category is usually determined from customizing, based on DGCI code (National classification code). However, if AssetReportFormCategory is entered into AssetMasterRecord, then it takes priority over the value from Customizing.&#10;If you use this field in your company code, link the validation keys BIOL and INVESTMENT to this field (Customizing view FIAAPTV_VAL_KEY).&#10;&#10;Type: Text&#10;Length: 80</Data></Cell>
    <Cell ss:StyleID="s113"><Data ss:Type="String">Is Amortized Asset Revaluated&#10;&#10;This is an indicator field. If the criterion is met, enter X. If not, leave the field empty.&#10;The field is used to determine which asset was revaluated at the time when it was completely depreciated. This is used to determine proper Asset Report Form (for example 3309 instead of 3310).&#10;If you use this field in your company code, link a validation key BENS_TOT_AMORT to this field (customizing view FIAAPTV_VAL_KEY).&#10;&#10;&#10;Type: Text&#10;Length: 1</Data></Cell>
    <Cell ss:StyleID="s113"><Data ss:Type="String">Exclusion Year&#10;&#10;Indicates the year when an asset was excluded from the tax depreciation group (the exclusion year).&#10;There is a special handling of assets acquired before fiscal year 2019 but excluded because of value increase postings.&#10;The depreciation of specific fixed assets acquired before 2019, is calculated at depreciation group level (rather than individually). However, if a fixed asset has a significant value increase, it is excluded from the group and depreciated individually, from the exclusion year.&#10;Use&#10;The exclusion year, compared with the reporting year (fiscal year derived from the Reporting date), is used to determine how an asset is reported:&#10;- Reporting year &lt;= Exclusion Year: an asset is relevant for Group depreciation calculation&#10;&#10;- Reporting year &gt;= Exclusion Year: an asset is relevant for Individual depreciation calculation&#10;The *A depreciation groups (for example, 2A or 3A) must be used for excluded assets.&#10;&#10;Type: Number&#10;Length: 4</Data></Cell>
    <Cell ss:StyleID="s113"><Data ss:Type="String">Last Invoice Date&#10;&#10;Indicates the date when the last invoice relevant for the fixed asset capitalization was posted.&#10;Use&#10;Usually, fixed assets with the capitalization date in fiscal year &gt;= 2019 are considered for Individual depreciation. However, if the Last invoice date is supplied by a date in fiscal year &lt; 2019, the asset will be still considered as relevant for group depreciation.&#10;Dependencies&#10;You use this field only if the fixed asset relevance for group/individual depreciation can't be determined based on the capitalization date.&#10;&#10;Type: Date</Data></Cell>
    <Cell ss:StyleID="s113"><Data ss:Type="String">National Classification Code&#10;&#10;In countries/regions which use the National Fixed Asset Classification Code, each fixed asset can be assigned to a specific National Classification Code. National Fixed Asset Classification Codes are published by the government.&#10;The National Classification Code provides the classification for industry and tax depreciation purposes.&#10;The National Fixed Asset Classification Code is used by reports which are issued to the Central Statistical Office and also for tax audit purposes.&#10;&#10;Type: Text&#10;Length: 80</Data></Cell>
    <Cell ss:StyleID="s113"><Data ss:Type="String">Tax Depreciation Group&#10;&#10;In countries/regions using the Tax Depreciation Group, each fixed asset can be assigned to a specific Tax Depreciation Group.&#10;The Tax Depreciation Group defines how long the asset is depreciated for tax purposes. The National Classification Code is used to determine the Tax Depreciation Group an asset belongs to.&#10;The Tax Depreciation Group is used by reports which are issued to the Central Statistical Office and also for Tax Audit purposes.&#10;Example&#10;A country/region may define specific Tax Depreciation Groups: Tax Depreciation Group 1 (4 years). Tax Depreciation Group 2 (6 years).&#10;&#10;Type: Text&#10;Length: 80</Data></Cell>

Make sure that unwanted leading zeros are not entered into the template.&#10;&#10;This key field, together with the Legacy Main Asset Number, uniquely identifies a fixed asset in the Legacy System.&#10;&#10;&#10;Key fields are mandatory and must always be filled with a unique key.&#10;If there is internal numbering, you can provide the key of your source system or any other unique key.&#10;The key is technically mandatory for the tool to internally connect the records of subordinated sheets with the records of the superordinated sheets.&#10;&#10;Type: Text&#10;Length: 4</Data></Cell>
    <Cell ss:StyleID="s113"><Data ss:Type="String">Depreciation Area Real or Derived*&#10;&#10;Depreciation area, which is managed in the system as a real depreciation area (not a derived depreciation area).&#10;&#10;Type: Text&#10;Length: 80</Data></Cell>
    <Cell ss:StyleID="s113"><Data ss:Type="String">(OBSOLETE) Date for Beginning of Valid.&#10;&#10;This field is obsolete and must not be used anymore.&#10;&#10;Type: Date</Data></Cell>

    <Cell ss:StyleID="s113"><Data ss:Type="String">SK Capital Improvement Year&#10;&#10;Fiscal year when a capital improvement is posted to a fixed asset, in accordance with the Slovak Income Tax Act.&#10;Capital improvements are usually posted as subsequent acquisitions or as acquiring transfers. Capital improvements cannot be posted in the first year of depreciation but can be posted in the second and subsequent years.&#10;&#10;You use capital improvement year in accelerated depreciation calculations, in the tax depreciation area of Slovak fixed assets.&#10;The system automatically determines the capital improvement year based on the transactional history. However, in some cases, such as legacy data transfers, you must manually specify the year. In these cases, you specify the most recent capital improvement year.&#10;Note: Capital improvement year has no impact on tax calculations involving the linear depreciation method.&#10;&#10;Type: Number&#10;Length: 4</Data></Cell>
